      <p>
       <b>
        Cádiz
       </b>
       (
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="'k' in 'kind'">
            k
           </span>
           <span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">
            ə
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'d' in 'dye'">
            d
           </span>
           <span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">
            ɪ
           </span>
           <span title="'z' in 'zoom'">
            z
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       ,
       <small>
        Spanish:
       </small>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">
         [ˈkaðiθ]
        </a>
       </span>
       ;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Collins3_1-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Collins3-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       see other pronunciations
       <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz#Toponymy" title="Cádiz">
        below
       </a>
       ) is a city and port in southwestern Spain. It is the capital of the province of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz_(province)" title="Cádiz (province)">
        Cádiz
       </a>
       , one of eight which make up the
       <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_communities_of_Spain" title="Autonomous communities of Spain">
        autonomous community
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">
        Andalusia
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Cádiz, regarded by many as the oldest continuously inhabited city in
       <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">
        Western Europe
       </a>
       , with archaeological remains dating to 3100  years,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-age1_2-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-age1-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pgou_3-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-pgou-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-age_4-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-age-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Independent_5-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-The_Independent-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       was founded by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phoenicians" title="Phoenicians">
        Phoenicians
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_6-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It has been a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naval_Structure_of_the_Spanish_Navy_in_the_New_Millennium" title="Naval Structure of the Spanish Navy in the New Millennium">
        principal home port of the Spanish Navy
       </a>
       since the accession of the
       <a href="/wiki/House_of_Bourbon" title="House of Bourbon">
        Spanish Bourbons
       </a>
       in the 18th century. The city is a member of the
       <a href="/wiki/Most_Ancient_European_Towns_Network" title="Most Ancient European Towns Network">
        Most Ancient European Towns Network
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Independent_5-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-The_Independent-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Members_7-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Members-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is also the site of the
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_C%C3%A1diz" title="University of Cádiz">
        University of Cádiz
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Situated on a narrow slice of land surrounded by the sea‚ Cádiz is, in most respects, a typically
       <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">
        Andalusian
       </a>
       city with a wealth of attractive vistas and well-preserved historical landmarks. The older part of Cádiz within the remnants of the
       <a href="/wiki/Defensive_wall" title="Defensive wall">
        city walls
       </a>
       is commonly referred to as the Old Town (Spanish:
       <i>
        Casco Antiguo
       </i>
       ). It is characterized by the antiquity of its various quarters (
       <i>
        barrios
       </i>
       ), among them
       <i>
        El Pópulo
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        La Viña
       </i>
       , and
       <i>
        Santa María
       </i>
       , which present a marked contrast to the newer areas of town. While the Old City's street plan consists of narrow winding alleys connecting large plazas, newer areas of Cádiz typically have wide avenues and more modern buildings. In addition, the city is dotted with numerous parks where
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exotic_plants" title="Exotic plants">
        exotic plants
       </a>
       flourish, including giant trees supposedly brought to Spain by
       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">
        Columbus
       </a>
       from the
       <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">
        New World
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Toponymy">
        Toponymy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=C%C3%A1diz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Toponymy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       <span id="etymology">
       </span>
       <span id="toponymy">
       </span>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vista_de_C%C3%A1diz,_Espa%C3%B1a,_2015-12-08,_DD_75-76_PAN.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3114" data-file-width="8745" height="78" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Vista_de_C%C3%A1diz%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2015-12-08%2C_DD_75-76_PAN.JPG/220px-Vista_de_C%C3%A1diz%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2015-12-08%2C_DD_75-76_PAN.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Vista_de_C%C3%A1diz%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2015-12-08%2C_DD_75-76_PAN.JPG/330px-Vista_de_C%C3%A1diz%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2015-12-08%2C_DD_75-76_PAN.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Vista_de_C%C3%A1diz%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2015-12-08%2C_DD_75-76_PAN.JPG/440px-Vista_de_C%C3%A1diz%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2015-12-08%2C_DD_75-76_PAN.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vista_de_C%C3%A1diz,_Espa%C3%B1a,_2015-12-08,_DD_75-76_PAN.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         General view
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mujeresplaya.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="271" data-file-width="500" height="119" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Mujeresplaya.jpg/220px-Mujeresplaya.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Mujeresplaya.jpg/330px-Mujeresplaya.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Mujeresplaya.jpg/440px-Mujeresplaya.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mujeresplaya.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Cádiz is mostly regarded by many as the oldest continuously inhabited city in Western Europe
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gades.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="642" data-file-width="984" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Gades.jpg/220px-Gades.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Gades.jpg/330px-Gades.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Gades.jpg/440px-Gades.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gades.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Satellite view of Cádiz
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Very little remains of the
       <a href="/wiki/Phoenician_language" title="Phoenician language">
        Phoenician language
       </a>
       , but
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Numismatic" title="Numismatic">
        numismatic
       </a>
       inscriptions record that they knew the site as
       <i>
        <span lang="phn-Latn" xml:lang="phn-Latn">
         a Gadir
        </span>
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        <span lang="phn-Latn" xml:lang="phn-Latn">
         Agadir
        </span>
       </i>
       (
       <span class="script-phoenician" dir="rtl" style="font-family: 'ALPHABETUM Unicode', 'MPH 2B Damase', Aegean, Code2001, 'Noto Sans Phoenician', FreeSans, 'Segoe UI Historic', sans-serif;" title="Phoenician alphabet">
        𐤀𐤂𐤃𐤓
       </span>
       ‬), meaning "The Wall", "The Compound", or (by
       <a href="/wiki/Metonymy" title="Metonymy">
        metonymy
       </a>
       ) "The Stronghold".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Borrowed by the
       <a href="/wiki/Berber_languages" title="Berber languages">
        Berber languages
       </a>
       , this became the
       <i>
        agadir
       </i>
       (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_Morocco_Tamazight" title="Central Morocco Tamazight">
        Tamazight
       </a>
       : "wall";
       <a href="/wiki/Shilha_language" title="Shilha language">
        Shilha
       </a>
       : "fortified granary") common in
       <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">
        North African
       </a>
       place names.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       (The Israeli town
       <a href="/wiki/Gedera" title="Gedera">
        Gedera
       </a>
       shares a similar etymology.) The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carthaginians" title="Carthaginians">
        Carthaginians
       </a>
       continued to use this name and all subsequent names have derived from it. The Greek
       <a href="/wiki/Cothon" title="Cothon">
        cothon
       </a>
       refers to a Carthaginian type of fortified basin that can be seen at ancient sites such as
       <a href="/wiki/Motya" title="Motya">
        Motya
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Attic_Greek" title="Attic Greek">
        Attic Greek
       </a>
       sources
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hellenized" title="Hellenized">
        hellenized
       </a>
       <i>
        Gadir
       </i>
       as
       <i>
        <span lang="grc-Latn" xml:lang="grc-Latn">
         tà Gádeira
        </span>
       </i>
       (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek_language" title="Ancient Greek language">
        Ancient Greek
       </a>
       :
       <span lang="grc" xml:lang="grc">
        τὰ Γάδειρα
       </span>
       ), which is neuter plural.
       <a href="/wiki/Herodotus" title="Herodotus">
        Herodotus
       </a>
       , using
       <a href="/wiki/Ionic_Greek" title="Ionic Greek">
        Ionic Greek
       </a>
       , transcribed it a little differently, as
       <i>
        <span lang="grc-Latn" xml:lang="grc-Latn">
         Gḗdeira
        </span>
       </i>
       (
       <span lang="grc" xml:lang="grc">
        Γήδειρα
       </span>
       ). Rarely, as in
       <a href="/wiki/Stephanus_of_Byzantium" title="Stephanus of Byzantium">
        Stephanus of Byzantium
       </a>
       's notes on the writings of
       <a href="/wiki/Eratosthenes" title="Eratosthenes">
        Eratosthenes
       </a>
       , the name is given in the feminine singular form as
       <i>
        <span lang="grc-Latn" xml:lang="grc-Latn">
         hè Gadeíra
        </span>
       </i>
       (
       <span lang="grc" xml:lang="grc">
        ἡ Γαδείρα
       </span>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       In Latin, the city was known as
       <i>
        <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">
         Gādēs
        </span>
       </i>
       and its Roman colony as
       <i>
        <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">
         Augusta Urbs Iulia Gaditana
        </span>
       </i>
       ("The August City of
       <a href="/wiki/Julia_(gens)" title="Julia (gens)">
        Julia
       </a>
       of Cádiz"). In
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">
        Arabic
       </a>
       , the Latin name became
       <i>
        <span lang="ar-Latn" xml:lang="ar-Latn">
         Qādis
        </span>
       </i>
       (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">
        Arabic
       </a>
       :
       <span dir="rtl" lang="ar" xml:lang="ar">
        قادس
       </span>
       ‎), from which the Spanish
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         Cádiz
        </span>
       </i>
       derives. The Spanish
       <a href="/wiki/Demonym" title="Demonym">
        demonym
       </a>
       for people and things from Cádiz is
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         gaditano
        </span>
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">
        English
       </a>
       , the name is pronounced variously. When the accent is on the second syllable, it is usually pronounced
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="'k' in 'kind'">
            k
           </span>
           <span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">
            ə
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'d' in 'dye'">
            d
           </span>
           <span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">
            ɪ
           </span>
           <span title="'z' in 'zoom'">
            z
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       but, when the accent is on the first syllable, it may be pronounced as
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'k' in 'kind'">
            k
           </span>
           <span title="/eɪ/: 'a' in 'face'">
            eɪ
           </span>
           <span title="'d' in 'dye'">
            d
           </span>
           <span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">
            ə
           </span>
           <span title="'z' in 'zoom'">
            z
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       , as
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'k' in 'kind'">
            k
           </span>
           <span title="/ɑː/: 'a' in 'father'">
            ɑː
           </span>
           <span title="'d' in 'dye'">
            d
           </span>
           <span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">
            ə
           </span>
           <span title="'z' in 'zoom'">
            z
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       , or as
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'k' in 'kind'">
            k
           </span>
           <span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">
            æ
           </span>
           <span title="'d' in 'dye'">
            d
           </span>
           <span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">
            ə
           </span>
           <span title="'z' in 'zoom'">
            z
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In Spanish, the accent is always on the first syllable but, while the usual pronunciation is
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">
         [ˈkaðiθ]
        </a>
       </span>
       , the local dialect says
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">
         [ˈkaðis]
        </a>
       </span>
       <small class="nowrap">
        (
        <span class="unicode haudio">
         <span class="fn">
          <span style="white-space:nowrap">
           <a href="/wiki/File:C%C3%A1diz-acento.ogg" title="About this sound">
            <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
           </a>
          </span>
          <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/cd/C%C3%A1diz-acento.ogg" title="Cádiz-acento.ogg">
           listen
          </a>
         </span>
        </span>
        )
       </small>
       ,
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">
         [ˈkaði]
        </a>
       </span>
       or
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">
         [ˈkai]
        </a>
       </span>
       instead. More recently, some English speakers
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hypercorrect" title="Hypercorrect">
        hypercorrect
       </a>
       and attempt to pronounce it as the Spanish, similarly to the British version of "
       <a href="/wiki/Ibiza#Name" title="Ibiza">
        Ibiza
       </a>
       ", leading to pronunciations of Cádiz with /s/ or /θ/ instead of /z/, but keeping the English vowels and the strong /d/.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">
        Demographics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=C%C3%A1diz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Demographics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       According to a 2016
       <a href="/wiki/Census" title="Census">
        census
       </a>
       estimate, the population of the city of Cádiz was 118.919 (the second most populated of the province after
       <a href="/wiki/Jerez_de_la_Frontera" title="Jerez de la Frontera">
        Jerez de la Frontera
       </a>
       with 212.830 inhabitants), and that of its
       <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area" title="Metropolitan area">
        metropolitan area
       </a>
       was 629,054. Cádiz is the seventeenth-largest Spanish city. In recent years, the city's population has steadily declined; it is the only municipality of the
       <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_C%C3%A1diz_(comarca)" title="Bay of Cádiz (comarca)">
        Bay of Cádiz
       </a>
       (the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Comarca" title="Comarca">
         comarca
        </a>
       </i>
       composed of Cádiz,
       <a href="/wiki/Chiclana_de_la_Frontera" title="Chiclana de la Frontera">
        Chiclana
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/El_Puerto_de_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa" title="El Puerto de Santa María">
        El Puerto de Santa María
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Real" title="Puerto Real">
        Puerto Real
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/San_Fernando,_C%C3%A1diz" title="San Fernando, Cádiz">
        San Fernando
       </a>
       ), whose population has diminished. Between 1995 and 2006, it lost more than 14,000 residents, a decrease of 9%.
      </p>
      <p>
       Among the causes of this loss of population is the peculiar geography of Cádiz; the city lies on a narrow spit of land hemmed in by the sea. Consequently, there is a pronounced shortage of land to be developed.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The city has very little vacant land, and a high proportion of its housing stock is relatively low in density.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       (That is to say, many buildings are only two or three stories tall, and they are only able to house a relatively small number of people within their "footprint".) The older quarters of Cádiz are full of buildings that, because of their age and historical significance, are not eligible for
       <a href="/wiki/Urban_renewal" title="Urban renewal">
        urban renewal
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <table style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;border:1px solid #999;border-collapse:collapse;background-color:#f3fff3">
       <caption style="margin-bottom:0.5em;font-size:1.1em;font-weight:bold">
        Historical population of Cádiz
        <br/>
        <small>
         (Source:
         <a class="external text" href="http://www.ine.es" rel="nofollow">
          INE (Spain)
         </a>
         )
        </small>
       </caption>
       <tr style="background:#ddffdd">
        <th scope="row" style="border:1px solid #999;padding:4px">
         Year
        </th>
        <th style="border:1px solid #999;padding:4px">
         1999
        </th>
        <th style="border:1px solid #999;padding:4px">
         2000
        </th>
        <th style="border:1px solid #999;padding:4px">
         2001
        </th>
        <th style="border:1px solid #999;padding:4px">
         2002
        </th>
        <th style="border:1px solid #999;padding:4px">
         2003
        </th>
        <th style="border:1px solid #999;padding:4px">
         2004
        </th>
        <th style="border:1px solid #999;padding:4px">
         2005
        </th>
        <th style="border:1px solid #999;padding:4px">
         2006
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th scope="row" style="border:1px solid #999;padding:4px">
         Population
        </th>
        <td style="border:1px solid #999;padding:4px;text-align:center">
         142,449
        </td>
        <td style="border:1px solid #999;padding:4px;text-align:center">
         140,061
        </td>
        <td style="border:1px solid #999;padding:4px;text-align:center">
         137,971
        </td>
        <td style="border:1px solid #999;padding:4px;text-align:center">
         136,236
        </td>
        <td style="border:1px solid #999;padding:4px;text-align:center">
         134,989
        </td>
        <td style="border:1px solid #999;padding:4px;text-align:center">
         133,242
        </td>
        <td style="border:1px solid #999;padding:4px;text-align:center">
         131,813
        </td>
        <td style="border:1px solid #999;padding:4px;text-align:center">
         130,561
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       Two other physical factors tend to limit the city's population. It is impossible to increase the amount of land available for building by reclaiming land from the sea; a new national law governing coastal development thwarts this possibility. Also, because Cádiz is built on a
       <a href="/wiki/Spit_(landform)" title="Spit (landform)">
        sandspit
       </a>
       , it is a costly proposition to sink foundations deep enough to support the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High-rise" title="High-rise">
        high-rise
       </a>
       buildings that would allow for a higher population density. As it stands, the city's
       <a href="/wiki/Skyline" title="Skyline">
        skyline
       </a>
       is not substantially different from in
       <a href="/wiki/Medieval_Times" title="Medieval Times">
        medieval times
       </a>
       . A 17th-century watchtower, the Tavira Tower, still commands a panoramic view of the city and the bay despite its relatively modest 45 meters (148 ft) height. (See below.)
      </p>
      <p>
       Cádiz is the provincial capital with the highest
       <a href="/wiki/Unemployment" title="Unemployment">
        rate of unemployment
       </a>
       in Spain. This, too, tends to depress the population level. Young Gaditanos, those between 18 and 30 years of age, have been migrating to other places in Spain (
       <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">
        Madrid
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Castell%C3%B3n_(province)" title="Castellón (province)">
        Castellón
       </a>
       , chiefly), as well as to other places in Europe and the Americas. The population younger than twenty years old is only 20.58% of the total, and the population older than sixty-five is 21.67%, making Cádiz one of the most aged cities in all of Spain.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Population_density">
        Population density
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=C%C3%A1diz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Population density">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The population distribution of the municipality is extremely uneven. In its inhabited areas, Cádiz is one of the most densely populated cities in Europe. The uninhabited Zona Franca industrial area, Bay of Cádiz Port Area, and Bay of Cádiz Natural Park occupy 63.63% of the municipal area. So the entire city population lives in the remaining 4.4 square kilometers (1.7 sq mi), at an average density close to 30,000 inhabitants per square kilometer. The city is divided for statistical purposes into 10 divisions, the most densely populated one having 39,592 inhabitants per square kilometer, the least having 20,835.
      </p>
      <p>
       The table below lists the area, population, and population density of the ten statistical divisions of Cádiz. Divisions 1 to 7, the "
       <i>
        stats divisions
       </i>
       ", belong to the old town; 8, 9 and 10 correspond to the "new city".
      </p>
