       </small>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=C%C3%A1diz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_C%C3%A1diz" title="Timeline of Cádiz">
        Timeline of Cádiz
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Founded in around 1104 BC as
       <i>
        Gadir
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        Agadir
       </i>
       by
       <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">
        Phoenicians
       </a>
       from
       <a href="/wiki/Tyre,_Lebanon" title="Tyre, Lebanon">
        Tyre
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_6-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Cádiz is mostly regarded as the most ancient city still standing in Western Europe.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-edad1_12-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-edad1-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The expeditions of
       <a href="/wiki/Himilco" title="Himilco">
        Himilco
       </a>
       around Spain and France and of
       <a href="/wiki/Hanno_the_Navigator" title="Hanno the Navigator">
        Hanno
       </a>
       around Western Africa began here. The Phoenician settlement traded with
       <a href="/wiki/Tartessos" title="Tartessos">
        Tartessos
       </a>
       , a city-state whose exact location remains unknown but is thought to have been somewhere near the mouth of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guadalquivir_River" title="Guadalquivir River">
        Guadalquivir River
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MuseoArqueologicoCadiz-P1050192.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/MuseoArqueologicoCadiz-P1050192.JPG/220px-MuseoArqueologicoCadiz-P1050192.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/MuseoArqueologicoCadiz-P1050192.JPG/330px-MuseoArqueologicoCadiz-P1050192.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/MuseoArqueologicoCadiz-P1050192.JPG/440px-MuseoArqueologicoCadiz-P1050192.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MuseoArqueologicoCadiz-P1050192.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Phoenician_sarcophagi_of_C%C3%A1diz&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Phoenician sarcophagi of Cádiz (page does not exist)">
          Phoenician sarcophagi found in Cádiz
         </a>
         , now in the Archaeological Museum of Cádiz; the sarcophagi is thought to have been imported from the Phoenician homeland around Sidon
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
          <a href="#cite_note-13">
           [13]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       One of the city's notable features during antiquity was the temple on the south end of its island dedicated to the Phoenician god
       <a href="/wiki/Melqart" title="Melqart">
        Melqart
       </a>
       , who was conflated with
       <a href="/wiki/Hercules" title="Hercules">
        Hercules
       </a>
       by the Greeks and Romans under the names "Tyrian Hercules" and "Hercules Gaditanus". It had an oracle and was famed for its wealth.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-willsmith_14-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-willsmith-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Greek_mythology" title="Greek mythology">
        Greek mythology
       </a>
       , Hercules was sometimes credited with founding
       <i>
        Gadeira
       </i>
       after performing his
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Labors_of_Hercules" title="Labors of Hercules">
        tenth labor
       </a>
       , the slaying of
       <a href="/wiki/Geryon" title="Geryon">
        Geryon
       </a>
       , a monster with three heads and torsos joined to a single pair of legs. (A
       <a href="/wiki/Tumulus" title="Tumulus">
        tumulus
       </a>
       near Gadeira was associated with Geryon's final resting-place.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       ) According to the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Life_of_Apollonius_of_Tyana" title="Life of Apollonius of Tyana">
         Life of Apollonius of Tyana
        </a>
       </i>
       , the "Heracleum" (i.e., the temple of Melqart) was still standing during the 1st century. Some historians, based in part on this source, believe that the columns of this temple were the origin of the myth of the "
       <a href="/wiki/Pillars_of_Hercules" title="Pillars of Hercules">
        pillars of Hercules
       </a>
       ".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Estatuillas_votivas_del_templo_de_H%C3%A9rcules_Gaditano.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="648" height="269" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Estatuillas_votivas_del_templo_de_H%C3%A9rcules_Gaditano.jpg/170px-Estatuillas_votivas_del_templo_de_H%C3%A9rcules_Gaditano.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Estatuillas_votivas_del_templo_de_H%C3%A9rcules_Gaditano.jpg/255px-Estatuillas_votivas_del_templo_de_H%C3%A9rcules_Gaditano.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Estatuillas_votivas_del_templo_de_H%C3%A9rcules_Gaditano.jpg/340px-Estatuillas_votivas_del_templo_de_H%C3%A9rcules_Gaditano.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Estatuillas_votivas_del_templo_de_H%C3%A9rcules_Gaditano.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Votive statues of Melqart-Hercules from the Islote de Sancti Petri
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The city fell under the sway of
       <a href="/wiki/Carthage" title="Carthage">
        Carthage
       </a>
       during
       <a href="/wiki/Hamilcar" title="Hamilcar">
        Hamilcar
       </a>
       's Iberian campaign after the
       <a href="/wiki/First_Punic_War" title="First Punic War">
        First Punic War
       </a>
       . Cádiz became a depot for
       <a href="/wiki/Hannibal" title="Hannibal">
        Hannibal
       </a>
       's conquest of southern
       <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">
        Iberia
       </a>
       , and he sacrificed there to Hercules/Melqart before setting off on his famous journey in 218 BC to cross the Alps and invade Italy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Later the city fell to
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">
        Romans
       </a>
       under
       <a href="/wiki/Scipio_Africanus" title="Scipio Africanus">
        Scipio Africanus
       </a>
       in 206 BC.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Under the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">
        Roman Republic
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">
        Empire
       </a>
       , the city flourished as a port and naval base known as
       <i>
        Gades
       </i>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Suetonius" title="Suetonius">
        Suetonius
       </a>
       relates how Julius Caesar, when visiting Gades as a
       <a href="/wiki/Quaestor" title="Quaestor">
        quaestor
       </a>
       (junior senator) saw a statue of Alexander the Great there and was saddened to think that he himself, though the same age, had still achieved nothing memorable.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The people of Gades had an alliance with Rome and
       <a href="/wiki/Julius_Caesar" title="Julius Caesar">
        Julius Caesar
       </a>
       bestowed
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_citizenship" title="Roman citizenship">
        Roman citizenship
       </a>
       on all its inhabitants in 49 BC.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-willsmith_14-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-willsmith-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By the time of
       <a href="/wiki/Augustus" title="Augustus">
        Augustus
       </a>
       's census, Cádiz was home to more than five hundred
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Equites" title="Equites">
         equites
        </a>
       </i>
       (members of the wealthy upper class), a concentration rivaled only by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Patavium" title="Patavium">
        Patavium
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Padua" title="Padua">
        Padua
       </a>
       ) and
       <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">
        Rome
       </a>
       itself.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It was the principal city of the
       <a href="/wiki/Colonies_in_antiquity" title="Colonies in antiquity">
        Roman colony
       </a>
       of Augusta Urbs Julia Gaditana. An
       <a href="/wiki/Aqueduct_(bridge)" title="Aqueduct (bridge)">
        aqueduct
       </a>
       provided fresh water to the town (the island's supply was notoriously bad), running across open sea for its last leg. However, Roman Gades was never very large. It consisted only of the northwest corner of the present island, and most of its wealthy citizens maintained estates outside of it on the
       <a href="/wiki/Castle_of_San_Sebasti%C3%A1n_(C%C3%A1diz)" title="Castle of San Sebastián (Cádiz)">
        nearby island
       </a>
       or on the mainland. The lifestyle maintained on the estates led to the Gaditan dancing girls becoming infamous throughout the ancient world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-willsmith_14-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-willsmith-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Although it is not in fact the most westerly city in the Spanish peninsula, for the Romans Cádiz had that reputation. The poet
       <a href="/wiki/Juvenal" title="Juvenal">
        Juvenal
       </a>
       begins his famous tenth satire with the words:
       <i>
        Omnibus in terris quae sunt a Gadibus usque Auroram et Gangen
       </i>
       ('In all the lands which exist from Gades as far as Dawn and the Ganges...').
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Military_history_of_Spain#The_collapse_of_Rome_and_barbarian_invasions" title="Military history of Spain">
        overthrow of Roman power
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Hispania_Baetica" title="Hispania Baetica">
        Hispania Baetica
       </a>
       by the
       <a href="/wiki/Visigoths" title="Visigoths">
        Visigoths
       </a>
       in 410 saw the destruction of the original city, of which there remain few remnants today. The site was later reconquered by Justinian in 551 as a part of the Byzantine province of
       <a href="/wiki/Spania" title="Spania">
        Spania
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It would remain Byzantine until Leovigild's reconquest in 572 returned it to the Visigothic Kingdom.
      </p>
      <p>
       Under
       <a href="/wiki/Moors" title="Moors">
        Moorish
       </a>
       rule between 711 and 1262, the city was called
       <i>
        Qādis
       </i>
       , whence the modern
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_naming_customs" title="Spanish naming customs">
        Spanish
       </a>
       name was derived. A famous Muslim legend developed concerning an "
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Idol_of_Cadiz&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Idol of Cadiz (page does not exist)">
        idol
       </a>
       " (
       <i>
        sanam Qādis
       </i>
       ) over 100
       <a href="/wiki/Cubit" title="Cubit">
        cubits
       </a>
       tall on the outskirts of Cádiz whose magic blocked the
       <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">
        strait of Gibraltar
       </a>
       with contrary winds and currents; its destruction by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abd-al-Mumin" title="Abd-al-Mumin">
        Abd-al-Mumin
       </a>
       c.
       <span style="white-space:nowrap;">
        1145
       </span>
       supposedly permitted ships to sail through the strait once more. It also appeared (as
       <i>
        Salamcadis
       </i>
       ) in the 12th-century
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turpin_(archbishop_of_Rheims)" title="Turpin (archbishop of Rheims)">
        Pseudo-Turpin
       </a>
       's
       <a href="/wiki/Historia_Caroli_Magni" title="Historia Caroli Magni">
        history of Charlemagne
       </a>
       , where it was considered a statue of
       <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">
        Muhammad
       </a>
       and thought to warn the Muslims of Christian invasion.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Classical sources are entirely silent on such a structure, but it has been conjectured that the origin of the legend was the ruins of a navigational aid constructed in
       <a href="/wiki/Late_antiquity" title="Late antiquity">
        late antiquity
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atat_24-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-atat-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Abd-al-Mumin (or Admiral Ali ibn-Isa ibn-Maymun) found that the idol was gilded bronze rather than pure gold, but coined what there was to help fund his revolt.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Moors were finally ousted by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alphonso_X" title="Alphonso X">
        Alphonso X
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">
        Castile
       </a>
       in 1262.
      </p>
      <p>
       During the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Age_of_Exploration" title="Age of Exploration">
        Age of Exploration
       </a>
       , the city experienced a renaissance.
       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">
        Christopher Columbus
       </a>
       sailed from Cádiz on his
       <a href="/wiki/Voyages_of_Christopher_Columbus" title="Voyages of Christopher Columbus">
        second and fourth voyages
       </a>
       and the city later became the home port of the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_treasure_fleet" title="Spanish treasure fleet">
        Spanish treasure fleet
       </a>
       . Consequently, it became a major target of Spain's enemies. The 16th century saw a series of failed raids by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barbary_corsairs" title="Barbary corsairs">
        Barbary corsairs
       </a>
       ; the greater part of the old town was consumed in a major fire in 1569; and in April, 1587, a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drake%27s_1587_expedition" title="Drake's 1587 expedition">
        raid
       </a>
       by the Englishman
       <a href="/wiki/Francis_Drake" title="Francis Drake">
        Francis Drake
       </a>
       occupied the harbor for three days, captured six ships, and destroyed 31 others (an event which became known in England as 'The Singeing of the
       <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain" title="Philip II of Spain">
        King of Spain
       </a>
       's Beard'). The attack delayed the sailing of the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Armada" title="Spanish Armada">
        Spanish Armada
       </a>
       by a year.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Francisco_de_Zurbar%C3%A1n_014.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2362" data-file-width="2564" height="203" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Francisco_de_Zurbar%C3%A1n_014.jpg/220px-Francisco_de_Zurbar%C3%A1n_014.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Francisco_de_Zurbar%C3%A1n_014.jpg/330px-Francisco_de_Zurbar%C3%A1n_014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Francisco_de_Zurbar%C3%A1n_014.jpg/440px-Francisco_de_Zurbar%C3%A1n_014.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Francisco_de_Zurbar%C3%A1n_014.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <i>
          Defense of Cádiz against the English
         </i>
         , by
         <a href="/wiki/Francisco_de_Zurbar%C3%A1n" title="Francisco de Zurbarán">
          Francisco de Zurbarán
         </a>
         , 1634 (Prado Museum, Madrid)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The city suffered a still more serious
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capture_of_Cadiz" title="Capture of Cadiz">
        attack in 1596
       </a>
       , when it was captured by another English fleet, this time under the Earls
       <a href="/wiki/Robert_Devereux,_2nd_Earl_of_Essex" title="Robert Devereux, 2nd Earl of Essex">
        of Essex
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Charles_Howard,_1st_Earl_of_Nottingham" title="Charles Howard, 1st Earl of Nottingham">
        Nottingham
       </a>
       . 32 Spanish ships were destroyed and the city was captured, looted and occupied for almost a month. Finally, when the royal authorities refused to pay a ransom demanded by the English for returning the city intact, they burned much of it before leaving with their booty. A third English raid was mounted against the city in 1625 by
       <a href="/wiki/George_Villiers,_1st_Duke_of_Buckingham" title="George Villiers, 1st Duke of Buckingham">
        George Villiers, 1st Duke of Buckingham
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Edward_Cecil,_1st_Viscount_Wimbledon" title="Edward Cecil, 1st Viscount Wimbledon">
        Edward Cecil
       </a>
       , but the attempt was unsuccessful. During the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglo-Spanish_War_(1654)" title="Anglo-Spanish War (1654)">
        Anglo-Spanish War
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Admiral_Robert_Blake" title="Admiral Robert Blake">
        Admiral Robert Blake
       </a>
       blockaded Cádiz from 1655 to 1657. In the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_C%C3%A1diz_(1702)" title="Battle of Cádiz (1702)">
        1702 Battle of Cádiz
       </a>
       , the English attacked again under
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_George_Rooke" title="Sir George Rooke">
        George Rooke
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/James_Butler,_2nd_Duke_of_Ormonde" title="James Butler, 2nd Duke of Ormonde">
        James Butler, 2nd Duke of Ormonde
       </a>
       , but they were repelled after a costly siege.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vista_de_C%C3%A1diz_y_sus_contornos_hacia_1813.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="809" data-file-width="900" height="198" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Vista_de_C%C3%A1diz_y_sus_contornos_hacia_1813.jpg/220px-Vista_de_C%C3%A1diz_y_sus_contornos_hacia_1813.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Vista_de_C%C3%A1diz_y_sus_contornos_hacia_1813.jpg/330px-Vista_de_C%C3%A1diz_y_sus_contornos_hacia_1813.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Vista_de_C%C3%A1diz_y_sus_contornos_hacia_1813.jpg/440px-Vista_de_C%C3%A1diz_y_sus_contornos_hacia_1813.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vista_de_C%C3%A1diz_y_sus_contornos_hacia_1813.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         1813 Map of Cádiz
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the 18th century, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sand_bar" title="Sand bar">
        sand bars
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Guadalquivir" title="Guadalquivir">
        Guadalquivir
       </a>
       forced the Spanish government to transfer its
       <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_America" title="Hispanic America">
        American
       </a>
       trade from
       <a href="/wiki/Seville" title="Seville">
        Seville
       </a>
       to Cádiz, which now commanded better access to the Atlantic. Although the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">
        empire
       </a>
       itself was declining, Cádiz now experienced another golden age from its new importance. It became one of Spain's greatest and most cosmopolitan cities and home to trading communities from many countries, the richest of which were the Irishmen.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Many of today's historic buildings in the Old City date from this era.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Plan_of_Cadiz.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="495" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Plan_of_Cadiz.jpg/220px-Plan_of_Cadiz.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Plan_of_Cadiz.jpg/330px-Plan_of_Cadiz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Plan_of_Cadiz.jpg/440px-Plan_of_Cadiz.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Plan_of_Cadiz.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Map of Cádiz, 1886
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       During the
       <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">
        Napoleonic Wars
       </a>
       , Cádiz was
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blockade_of_C%C3%A1diz_(1797)" title="Blockade of Cádiz (1797)">
        blockaded by the British
       </a>
       from 1797 until the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peace_of_Amiens" title="Peace of Amiens">
        Peace of Amiens
       </a>
       in 1802 and again from 1803 until the outbreak of the
       <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_War" title="Peninsular War">
        Peninsular War
       </a>
       in 1808. In that war, it was one of the few Spanish cities to hold out against the invading French and their candidate
       <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Bonaparte" title="Joseph Bonaparte">
        Joseph Bonaparte
       </a>
       . Cádiz then became the seat of Spain's military high command and
       <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz_Cortes" title="Cádiz Cortes">
        Cortes
       </a>
       (parliament) for the duration of the war. It was here that the liberal
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Constitution_of_1812" title="Spanish Constitution of 1812">
        Spanish Constitution of 1812
       </a>
       was proclaimed. The citizens revolted in 1820 to secure a renewal of this constitution and the revolution spread successfully until
       <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_VII_of_Spain" title="Ferdinand VII of Spain">
        Ferdinand VII
       </a>
       was imprisoned in Cádiz.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_France" title="Military of France">
        French forces
       </a>
       secured the release of Ferdinand in the 1823
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Trocadero" title="Battle of Trocadero">
        Battle of Trocadero
       </a>
       and suppressed liberalism for a time. In 1868, Cádiz was once again the seat of a revolution, resulting in the eventual abdication and exile of Queen
       <a href="/wiki/Isabella_II_of_Spain" title="Isabella II of Spain">
        Isabella II
       </a>
       . The Cádiz Cortes decided to reinstate the monarchy under King
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amadeo_of_Spain" title="Amadeo of Spain">
        Amadeo
       </a>
       just two years later.
      </p>
      <p>
       In recent years, the city has undergone much reconstruction. Many monuments, cathedrals, and
       <a href="/wiki/Landmark" title="Landmark">
        landmarks
       </a>
       have been cleaned and restored.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Diocese">
        Diocese
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=C%C3%A1diz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Diocese">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Cadiz_y_Ceuta" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Cadiz y Ceuta">
        Roman Catholic Diocese of Cadiz y Ceuta
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The diocese of Cádiz and
       <a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">
        Ceuta
       </a>
       is a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suffragan" title="Suffragan">
        suffragan
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Seville" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Seville">
        Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Seville
       </a>
       ; that is, it is a diocese within the metropolitan see of Seville. It became a diocese in 1263 after its
       <a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">
        Reconquista
       </a>
       (reconquest) from the Moors. By the
       <a href="/wiki/Concordat" title="Concordat">
        Concordat
       </a>
       of 1753, in which the Spanish crown also gained the rights to make appointments to church offices and to tax church lands, the diocese of Cádiz was merged with the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Ceuta" title="Diocese of Ceuta">
        diocese of Ceuta
       </a>
       , a Spanish conclave on the northern coast of Africa, and the
       <a href="/wiki/Diocesan_bishop" title="Diocesan bishop">
        diocesan bishop
       </a>
       became, by virtue of his office, the
       <a href="/wiki/Apostolic_Administrator" title="Apostolic Administrator">
        Apostolic Administrator
       </a>
       of Ceuta.
      </p>
      <p>
       Historically, the diocese counts among its most famous prelates
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Juan_de_Torquemada_(Cardinal)" title="Juan de Torquemada (Cardinal)">
        Cardinal Juan de Torquemada
       </a>
       , a
       <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Order" title="Dominican Order">
        Dominican
       </a>
       theologian and expert on
       <a href="/wiki/Canon_law" title="Canon law">
        canon law
       </a>
       , who took a leading part in the Councils of Basle and Florence, and defended, in his
       <i>
        Summe de Ecclesia
       </i>
       , the direct power of the pope in temporal matters. His nephew,
       <a href="/wiki/Tom%C3%A1s_de_Torquemada" title="Tomás de Torquemada">
        Tomás de Torquemada
       </a>
       , is most closely associated with the 15th century
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Inquisition" title="Spanish Inquisition">
        Spanish Inquisition
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Main_sights">
        Main sights
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=C%C3%A1diz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Main sights">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Among the many landmarks of historical and scenic interest in Cádiz, a few stand out. The city can boast of an unusual cathedral of various
       <a href="/wiki/Architectural_style" title="Architectural style">
        architectural styles
       </a>
       , a theater, an old municipal building, an 18th-century watchtower, a vestige of the ancient city wall, an ancient Roman theater, and electrical pylons of an eye-catchingly modern design carrying cables across the Bay of Cádiz. The old town is characterized by narrow streets connecting squares (
       <i>
        plazas
       </i>
       ), bordered by the sea and by the city walls. Most of the landmark buildings are situated in the plazas.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Plazas_and_their_landmark_buildings">
        Plazas and their landmark buildings
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=C%C3%A1diz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Plazas and their landmark buildings">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The old town of Cádiz is one of the most densely populated urban areas in Europe
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       and is packed with narrow streets. The old town benefits, though, from several striking plazas, which are enjoyed by citizens and tourists alike. These are the
       <i>
        Plaza de Mina
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Plaza San Antonio
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Plaza de Candelaria
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Plaza de San Juan de Dios
       </i>
       , and
       <i>
        Plaza de España
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Plaza_de_Mina">
        Plaza de Mina
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=C%C3%A1diz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Plaza de Mina">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Located in the heart of the old town, Plaza de Mina was developed in the first half of the 19th century. Previously, the land occupied by the plaza was the orchard of the convent of San Francisco. The plaza was converted into a plaza in 1838 by the architect Torcuato Benjumeda and (later) Juan Daura, with its trees being planted in 1861. It was then redeveloped again in 1897, and has remained virtually unchanged since that time. It is named after General
       <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Espoz_y_Mina" title="Francisco Espoz y Mina">
        Francisco Espoz y Mina
       </a>
       , a hero of the war of independence.
       <a href="/wiki/Manuel_de_Falla" title="Manuel de Falla">
        Manuel de Falla
       </a>
       y Matheu was born in Number 3 Plaza de Mina, where a plaque bears his name. The plaza also contains several statues, one of these is a bust of José Macpherson (a pioneer in the development of
       <a href="/wiki/Petrography" title="Petrography">
        petrography
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Stratigraphy" title="Stratigraphy">
        stratigraphy
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Tectonics" title="Tectonics">
        tectonics
       </a>
       ) who was born in number 12 Plaza de Mina in 1839. The
       <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_C%C3%A1diz" title="Museum of Cádiz">
        Museum of Cádiz
       </a>
       , is to be found at number 5 Plaza de Mina, and contains many objects from Cádiz's 3000-year history as well as works by artists such as
       <a href="/wiki/Peter_Paul_Rubens" title="Peter Paul Rubens">
        Peter Paul Rubens
       </a>
       . The houses which face the plaza, many of which can be classified as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neo-classical_architecture" title="Neo-classical architecture">
        neo-classical architecture
       </a>
       or built in the style of
       <a href="/wiki/Isabelline_Gothic" title="Isabelline Gothic">
        Isabelline Gothic
       </a>
       , were originally occupied by the Cádiz
       <a href="/wiki/Bourgeoisie" title="Bourgeoisie">
        bourgeoisie
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The Plaza de la Catedral houses both the Cathedral and the
       <a href="/wiki/Baroque_architecture" title="Baroque architecture">
        Baroque
       </a>
       church of
       <i>
        Santiago
       </i>
       , built in 1635.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Plaza_de_San_Francisco_and_San_Francisco_Church_and_Convent">
        Plaza de San Francisco and San Francisco Church and Convent
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=C%C3%A1diz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Plaza de San Francisco and San Francisco Church and Convent">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:San_Antonio_church_263.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/San_Antonio_church_263.jpg/220px-San_Antonio_church_263.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/San_Antonio_church_263.jpg/330px-San_Antonio_church_263.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/San_Antonio_church_263.jpg/440px-San_Antonio_church_263.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:San_Antonio_church_263.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         San Francisco church
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Located next to Plaza de Mina, this smaller square houses the San Francisco church and convent. Originally built in 1566, it was substantially renovated in the 17th century,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cadiz2_27-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cadiz2-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       when its cloisters were added.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EspanaFascinante2012_28-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-EspanaFascinante2012-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Originally, the Plaza de Mina formed the convent's orchard.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Plaza_San_Antonio">
        Plaza San Antonio
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=C%C3%A1diz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Plaza San Antonio">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iglesia_de_San_Antonio_de_Padua,_C%C3%A1diz.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3440" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Iglesia_de_San_Antonio_de_Padua%2C_C%C3%A1diz.jpg/220px-Iglesia_de_San_Antonio_de_Padua%2C_C%C3%A1diz.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Iglesia_de_San_Antonio_de_Padua%2C_C%C3%A1diz.jpg/330px-Iglesia_de_San_Antonio_de_Padua%2C_C%C3%A1diz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Iglesia_de_San_Antonio_de_Padua%2C_C%C3%A1diz.jpg/440px-Iglesia_de_San_Antonio_de_Padua%2C_C%C3%A1diz.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Iglesia_de_San_Antonio_de_Padua,_C%C3%A1diz.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Plaza de San Antonio and church
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the 19th century Plaza San Antonio was considered to be Cádiz's main square. The square is surrounded by a number of mansions built in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neo-classical_architecture" title="Neo-classical architecture">
        neo-classical architecture
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Isabelline_Gothic" title="Isabelline Gothic">
        Isabelline Gothic
       </a>
       style, once occupied by the Cádiz upper classes. San Antonio church, originally built in 1669, is also situated in the plaza.
      </p>
      <p>
       The plaza was built in the 18th century, and on 19 March 1812 the Spanish
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constitution_of_1812" title="Constitution of 1812">
        Constitution of 1812
       </a>
       was proclaimed here, leading to the plaza to be named Plaza de la Constitución, and then later Plaza San Antonio, after the hermit San Antonio.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1954 the city's mayor proclaimed the location a historic site. All construction is prohibited.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Plaza_de_Candelaria">
        Plaza de Candelaria
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=C%C3%A1diz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Plaza de Candelaria">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The Plaza de Candelaria is named after the Candelaria convent, situated in the square until it was demolished in 1873, when its grounds were redeveloped as a plaza. The plaza is notable for a statue in its centre of
       <a href="/wiki/Emilio_Castelar" title="Emilio Castelar">
        Emilio Castelar
       </a>
       , president of the first Spanish republic, who was born in a house facing the square. A plaque situated on another house, states that
       <a href="/wiki/Bernardo_O%27Higgins" title="Bernardo O'Higgins">
        Bernardo O'Higgins
       </a>
       , an Irish-Chilean adventurer and former dictator of Chile also, lived in the square.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Plaza_de_la_Catedral_and_the_Cathedral">
        Plaza de la Catedral and the Cathedral
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=C%C3%A1diz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Plaza de la Catedral and the Cathedral">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz_Cathedral" title="Cádiz Cathedral">
        Cádiz Cathedral
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cathedrale_de_Cadiz.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Cathedrale_de_Cadiz.jpg/220px-Cathedrale_de_Cadiz.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Cathedrale_de_Cadiz.jpg/330px-Cathedrale_de_Cadiz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Cathedrale_de_Cadiz.jpg/440px-Cathedrale_de_Cadiz.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cathedrale_de_Cadiz.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz_Cathedral" title="Cádiz Cathedral">
          Cádiz Cathedral
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       One of Cádiz's most famous landmarks is its cathedral. It sits on the site of an older cathedral, completed in 1260, which burned down in 1596. The reconstruction, which was not started until 1776, was supervised by the architect
       <a href="/wiki/Vicente_Acero" title="Vicente Acero">
        Vicente Acero
       </a>
       , who had also built the
       <a href="/wiki/Granada_Cathedral" title="Granada Cathedral">
        Granada Cathedral
       </a>
       . Acero left the project and was succeeded by several other architects. As a result, this largely Baroque-style cathedral was built over a period of 116 years, and, due to this drawn-out period of construction, the cathedral underwent several major changes to its original design. Though the cathedral was originally intended to be a baroque edifice, it contains
       <a href="/wiki/Rococo" title="Rococo">
        rococo
       </a>
       elements, and was completed in the
       <a href="/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture" title="Neoclassical architecture">
        neoclassical style
       </a>
       . Its
       <a href="/wiki/Chapel" title="Chapel">
        chapels
       </a>
       have many paintings and relics from the old cathedral and monasteries from throughout Spain.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Plaza_de_San_Juan_de_Dios_and_the_Old_Town_Hall">
        Plaza de San Juan de Dios and the Old Town Hall
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=C%C3%A1diz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Plaza de San Juan de Dios and the Old Town Hall">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ayuntamiento_145.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Ayuntamiento_145.jpg/220px-Ayuntamiento_145.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Ayuntamiento_145.jpg/330px-Ayuntamiento_145.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Ayuntamiento_145.jpg/440px-Ayuntamiento_145.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ayuntamiento_145.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Ayuntamiento
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Construction of this plaza began in the 15th century on lands reclaimed from the sea. With the demolition of the City walls in 1906 the plaza increased in size and a statue of the Cádiz politician Segismundo Moret was unveiled. Overlooking the plaza, the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Ayuntamiento" title="Ayuntamiento">
         Ayuntamiento
        </a>
       </i>
       is the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Town_hall" title="Town hall">
        town hall
       </a>
       of Cádiz's
       <i>
        Old City
       </i>
       . The structure, constructed on the bases and location of the previous
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Consistorial_Houses&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Consistorial Houses (page does not exist)">
        Consistorial Houses
       </a>
       (1699), was built in two stages. The first stage began in 1799 under the direction of architect
       <a href="/wiki/Torcuato_Benjumeda" title="Torcuato Benjumeda">
        Torcuato Benjumeda
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture" title="Neoclassical architecture">
        neoclassical
       </a>
       style. The second stage was completed in 1861 under the direction of
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Garc%C3%ADa_del_Alamo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="García del Alamo (page does not exist)">
        García del Alamo
       </a>
       , in the
       <a href="/wiki/Isabelline_Gothic" title="Isabelline Gothic">
        Isabelline Gothic
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         Gótico Isabelino
        </span>
       </i>
       or, simply, the
       <i>
        Isabelino
       </i>
       ) style. Here, in 1936, the flag of
       <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">
        Andalusia
       </a>
       was hoisted for the first time.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span id="Plaza_de_Espa.C3.B1a_and_the_monument_to_the_constitution_of_1812">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Plaza_de_España_and_the_monument_to_the_constitution_of_1812">
        Plaza de España and the monument to the constitution of 1812
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=C%C3%A1diz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Plaza de España and the monument to the constitution of 1812">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This section
          <b>
           does not
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">
            cite
           </a>
           any
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
            sources
           </a>
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please help
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=C%C3%A1diz&amp;action=edit">
            improve this section
           </a>
           by
           <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">
            adding citations to reliable sources
           </a>
           . Unsourced material may be challenged and
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
            removed
           </a>
           .
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (May 2013)
           </i>
          </small>
          <small class="hide-when-compact">
           <i>

            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">
             Learn how and when to remove this template message
            </a>
            )
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Monumento_a_las_Cortes_de_C%C3%A1diz,_mayo_de_2009.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3968" data-file-width="2976" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Monumento_a_las_Cortes_de_C%C3%A1diz%2C_mayo_de_2009.jpg/220px-Monumento_a_las_Cortes_de_C%C3%A1diz%2C_mayo_de_2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Monumento_a_las_Cortes_de_C%C3%A1diz%2C_mayo_de_2009.jpg/330px-Monumento_a_las_Cortes_de_C%C3%A1diz%2C_mayo_de_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Monumento_a_las_Cortes_de_C%C3%A1diz%2C_mayo_de_2009.jpg/440px-Monumento_a_las_Cortes_de_C%C3%A1diz%2C_mayo_de_2009.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Monumento_a_las_Cortes_de_C%C3%A1diz,_mayo_de_2009.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Monument to the Constitution of 1812
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Plaza de España is a large square close to the port. It is dominated by the
       <i>
        Monument to the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constitution_of_1812" title="Constitution of 1812">
         Constitution of 1812
        </a>
       </i>
       , which came into being as a consequence of the demolition of a portion of the old city wall. The plaza is an extension of the old
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Plazuela_del_Carb%C3%B3n&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Plazuela del Carbón (page does not exist)">
        Plazuela del Carbón
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The goal of this demolition was to create a grand new city square to mark the hundredth anniversary of the liberal constitution, which was proclaimed in this city in 1812, and provide a setting for a suitable memorial. The work is by the architect,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Modesto_Lopez_Otero" title="Modesto Lopez Otero">
        Modesto Lopez Otero
       </a>
       , and of the sculptor,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Aniceto_Marinas&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Aniceto Marinas (page does not exist)">
        Aniceto Marinas
       </a>
       . The work began in 1912 and finished in 1929.
      </p>
      <p>
       The lower level of the monument represents a chamber and an empty presidential armchair. The upper level has various inscriptions surmounting the chamber. On each side are bronze figures representing peace and war. In the centre, a
       <a href="/wiki/Pilaster" title="Pilaster">
        pilaster
       </a>
       rises to symbolize, in allegorical terms, the principles expressed in the 1812 constitution. At the foot of this pilaster, there is a female figure representing Spain, and, to either side, sculptural groupings representing agriculture and citizenship.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span id="Plaza_de_Falla_and_the_Gran_Teatro_Falla_.28Falla_Grand_Theater.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Plaza_de_Falla_and_the_Gran_Teatro_Falla_(Falla_Grand_Theater)">
        Plaza de Falla and the Gran Teatro Falla (Falla Grand Theater)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=C%C3%A1diz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Plaza de Falla and the Gran Teatro Falla (Falla Grand Theater)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The original
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Gran_Teatro_Falla" title="Gran Teatro Falla">
         Gran Teatro
        </a>
       </i>
       was constructed in 1871 by the architect García del Alamo, and was destroyed by a fire in August 1881. The current theater was built between 1884 and 1905 over the remains of the previous Gran Teatro. The architect was Adolfo Morales de los Rios, and the overseer of construction was Juan Cabrera de la Torre. The outside was covered in red
       <a href="/wiki/Brick" title="Brick">
        bricks
       </a>
       and is of a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neo_Mud%C3%A9jar" title="Neo Mudéjar">
        neo-Mudéjar
       </a>
       or
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moorish_Revival" title="Moorish Revival">
        Moorish revival
       </a>
       style. Following renovations in the 1920s, the theater was renamed the
       <i>
        Gran Teatro Falla
       </i>
       , in honor of composer
       <a href="/wiki/Manuel_de_Falla" title="Manuel de Falla">
        Manuel de Falla
       </a>
       , who is buried in the crypt of the cathedral. After a period of disrepair in the 1980s, the theater has since undergone extensive renovation.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_sights">
        Other sights
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=C%C3%A1diz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Other sights">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tavira_tower">
        Tavira tower
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=C%C3%A1diz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Tavira tower">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       In the 18th century, Cádiz had more than 160 towers from which local merchants could look out to sea for arriving
       <a href="/wiki/Cargo_ship" title="Cargo ship">
        merchant ships
       </a>
       . These towers often formed part of the merchants' houses. The
       <i>
        Torre Tavira
       </i>
       , named for its original owner, stands as the tallest remaining watchtower. It has a
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Camera_obscura" title="Camera obscura">
         camera obscura
        </a>
       </i>
       , a room that uses the principle of the
       <a href="/wiki/Pinhole_camera" title="Pinhole camera">
        pinhole camera
       </a>
       and a specially prepared
       <a href="/wiki/Lens_(optics)" title="Lens (optics)">
        convex lens
       </a>
       to project panoramic views of the Old City onto a concave disc.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span id="Admiral.27s_House">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Admiral's_House">
        Admiral's House
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=C%C3%A1diz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Admiral's House">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Admiral%27s_House_161.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3872" data-file-width="2592" height="329" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Admiral%27s_House_161.jpg/220px-Admiral%27s_House_161.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Admiral%27s_House_161.jpg/330px-Admiral%27s_House_161.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Admiral%27s_House_161.jpg/440px-Admiral%27s_House_161.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Admiral%27s_House_161.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Admiral's House
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <i>
        Casa del Almirante
       </i>
       is a palatial house, adjacent to the Plaza San Martín in the Barrio del Pópulo, which was constructed in 1690 with the proceeds of the lucrative trade with the Americas. It was built by the family of the admiral of the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_treasure_fleet" title="Spanish treasure fleet">
        Spanish treasure fleet
       </a>
       , the so-called
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Fleet_of_the_Indies&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Fleet of the Indies (page does not exist)">
        Fleet of the Indies
       </a>
       , Don
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Diego_de_Barrios&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Diego de Barrios (page does not exist)">
        Diego de Barrios
       </a>
       . The exterior is sheathed in exquisite red and white Genoan marble, prepared in the workshops of Andreoli, and mounted by the master,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Garc%C3%ADa_Narv%C3%A1ez&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="García Narváez (page does not exist)">
        García Narváez
       </a>
       . The colonnaded portico, the grand staircase under the cupola, and the hall on the main floor are architectural features of great nobility and beauty. The shield of the Barrios family appears on the second-floor balcony.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Old_customs_house">
        Old customs house
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=C%C3%A1diz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Old customs house">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Situated within the confines of the walls which protect the flank of the port of Cádiz are three identical adjacent buildings: the Customs House, the House of Hiring and the Consulate. Of the three, the former had been erected first, built in a sober neo-classical style and of ample and balanced proportions. The works began in 1765 under the direction of Juan Caballero at a cost of 7,717,200
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_real" title="Spanish real">
        reales
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Palacio_de_Congresos">
        Palacio de Congresos
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=C%C3%A1diz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Palacio de Congresos">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Cádiz's refurbished tobacco factory offers international conference and trade-show facilities.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-palaciocongresos-cadiz_29-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-palaciocongresos-cadiz-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Home to the third annual MAST Conference and trade-show (12 to 14 November 2008)
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Roman_theatre">
        Roman theatre
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=C%C3%A1diz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Roman theatre">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Teatro_Romano_de_C%C3%A1diz_-_Grader%C3%ADo.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="1728" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Teatro_Romano_de_C%C3%A1diz_-_Grader%C3%ADo.JPG/220px-Teatro_Romano_de_C%C3%A1diz_-_Grader%C3%ADo.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Teatro_Romano_de_C%C3%A1diz_-_Grader%C3%ADo.JPG/330px-Teatro_Romano_de_C%C3%A1diz_-_Grader%C3%ADo.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Teatro_Romano_de_C%C3%A1diz_-_Grader%C3%ADo.JPG/440px-Teatro_Romano_de_C%C3%A1diz_-_Grader%C3%ADo.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Teatro_Romano_de_C%C3%A1diz_-_Grader%C3%ADo.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Roman theatre
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Theatre_(C%C3%A1diz)" title="Roman Theatre (Cádiz)">
        Roman Theatre (Cádiz)
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Roman theatre was discovered in 1980, in the El Pópulo district, after a fire had destroyed some old warehouses, revealing a layer of construction that was judged to be the foundations of some medieval buildings; the foundations of these buildings had been built, in turn, upon much more ancient stones, hand-hewn limestone of a Roman character. Systematic excavations have revealed a largely intact Roman theatre.
      </p>
      <p>
       The theatre, constructed by order of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lucius_Cornelius_Balbus_(minor)" title="Lucius Cornelius Balbus (minor)">
        Lucius Cornelius Balbus (minor)
       </a>
       during the 1st century BC, is the second-largest Roman theatre in the world, surpassed only by the theatre of
       <a href="/wiki/Pompeii" title="Pompeii">
        Pompeii
       </a>
       , south of
       <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">
        Rome
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Cicero" title="Cicero">
        Cicero
       </a>
       , in his
       <i>
        Epistulae ad Familiares
       </i>
       ('Letters to his friends'), wrote of its use by Balbus for personal propaganda.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span id="Pylons_of_C.C3.A1diz">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Pylons_of_Cádiz">
        Pylons of Cádiz
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=C%C3%A1diz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Pylons of Cádiz">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pilones_de_C%C3%A1diz,_mayo_de_2009.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3968" data-file-width="2976" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Pilones_de_C%C3%A1diz%2C_mayo_de_2009.jpg/220px-Pilones_de_C%C3%A1diz%2C_mayo_de_2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Pilones_de_C%C3%A1diz%2C_mayo_de_2009.jpg/330px-Pilones_de_C%C3%A1diz%2C_mayo_de_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Pilones_de_C%C3%A1diz%2C_mayo_de_2009.jpg/440px-Pilones_de_C%C3%A1diz%2C_mayo_de_2009.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pilones_de_C%C3%A1diz,_mayo_de_2009.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Pylons of Cádiz
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Pylons_of_C%C3%A1diz" title="Pylons of Cádiz">
        Pylons of Cádiz
       </a>
       are
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electricity_pylon" title="Electricity pylon">
        electricity pylons
       </a>
       of unusual design, one on either side of the
       <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_C%C3%A1diz" title="Bay of Cádiz">
        Bay of Cádiz
       </a>
       , used to support huge electric-power cables. The pylons are 158 meters (518 ft) high and designed for two
       <a href="/wiki/Electrical_network" title="Electrical network">
        circuits
       </a>
       . The very unconventional construction consists of a narrow
       <a href="/wiki/Frustum" title="Frustum">
        frustum
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Steel" title="Steel">
        steel
       </a>
       framework with one crossbar at the top of each one for the insulators.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Carranza_Bridge">
        Carranza Bridge
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=C%C3%A1diz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Carranza Bridge">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Leon_de_Carranza_Bridge" title="José Leon de Carranza Bridge">
        José Leon de Carranza Bridge
       </a>
      </div>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="La_Pepa_Bridge">
        La Pepa Bridge
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=C%C3%A1diz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: La Pepa Bridge">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/La_Pepa_Bridge" title="La Pepa Bridge">
        La Pepa Bridge
       </a>
       , officially "La Pepa" and also named the second bridge to Cádiz or new access to Cádiz. It opened 24 September 2015. It crosses the
       <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_C%C3%A1diz" title="Bay of Cádiz">
        Bay of Cádiz
       </a>
       linking Cádiz with
       <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Real" title="Puerto Real">
        Puerto Real
       </a>
       in mainland Spain. It is the longest bridge in Spain and the longest span cable-stayed in the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="City_walls_and_fortifications">
        City walls and fortifications
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=C%C3%A1diz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: City walls and fortifications">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:19Jmani_C%C3%A1diz_0073.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/19Jmani_C%C3%A1diz_0073.jpg/220px-19Jmani_C%C3%A1diz_0073.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/19Jmani_C%C3%A1diz_0073.jpg/330px-19Jmani_C%C3%A1diz_0073.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/19Jmani_C%C3%A1diz_0073.jpg/440px-19Jmani_C%C3%A1diz_0073.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:19Jmani_C%C3%A1diz_0073.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Las puertas de tierra
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <i>
        Las Puertas de Tierra
       </i>
       originated in the 16th century,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       although much of the original work has disappeared. Once consisting of several layers of walls, only one of these remain today. By the 20th century it was necessary to remodel the entrance to the Old City to accommodate modern traffic. Today, the two side-by-side arches cut into the wall serve as one of the primary entrances to the city.
      </p>
      <p>
       <i>
        El Arco de los Blancos
       </i>
       is the gate to the Populo district, built around 1300. It was the principal gate to the medieval town. The gate is named after the family of Felipe Blanco who built a chapel (now disappeared) above the gate.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arco-de-la-rosa.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1041" data-file-width="700" height="327" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Arco-de-la-rosa.jpg/220px-Arco-de-la-rosa.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Arco-de-la-rosa.jpg/330px-Arco-de-la-rosa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Arco-de-la-rosa.jpg/440px-Arco-de-la-rosa.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Arco-de-la-rosa.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Arco de la Rosa
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <i>
        El Arco de la Rosa
       </i>
       ("Rose Arch") is a gate carved into the medieval walls next to the cathedral. It is named after captain Gaspar de la Rosa, who lived in the city during the 18th century. The gate was renovated in 1973.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <i>
        Baluarte de la Candelaria
       </i>
       (fortress or stronghold of
       <a href="/wiki/Presentation_of_Jesus_at_the_Temple" title="Presentation of Jesus at the Temple">
        Candlemas
       </a>
       ) is a military fortification. Taking advantage of a natural elevation of land, it was constructed in 1672 at the initiative of the governor,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Diego_Caballero_de_Illescas&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Diego Caballero de Illescas (page does not exist)">
        Diego Caballero de Illescas
       </a>
       . Protected by a seaward-facing wall that had previously served as a seawall, Candelaria's cannons were in a position to command the channels approaching the port of Cádiz. In more recent times, the edifice has served as a headquarters for the corps of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_engineer" title="Military engineer">
        military engineers
       </a>
       and as the home to the army's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Homing_pigeons" title="Homing pigeons">
        homing pigeons
       </a>
       , birds used to carry written messages over hostile terrain. Thoroughly renovated, it is now used as a cultural venue. There has been some discussion of using it to house a
       <a href="/wiki/Maritime_museum" title="Maritime museum">
        maritime museum
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       but, at present, it is designated for use as a permanent exposition space.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Castle_of_San_Sebasti%C3%A1n_(C%C3%A1diz)" title="Castle of San Sebastián (Cádiz)">
         Castle of San Sebastián
        </a>
       </i>
       is also a military fortification and is situated at the end of a road leading out from the Caleta beach. It was built in 1706. Today the castle remains unused, although its future uses remain much debated.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Castillo_de_Santa_Catalina_5,_C%C3%A1diz.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3968" data-file-width="2976" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Castillo_de_Santa_Catalina_5%2C_C%C3%A1diz.jpg/220px-Castillo_de_Santa_Catalina_5%2C_C%C3%A1diz.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Castillo_de_Santa_Catalina_5%2C_C%C3%A1diz.jpg/330px-Castillo_de_Santa_Catalina_5%2C_C%C3%A1diz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Castillo_de_Santa_Catalina_5%2C_C%C3%A1diz.jpg/440px-Castillo_de_Santa_Catalina_5%2C_C%C3%A1diz.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Castillo_de_Santa_Catalina_5,_C%C3%A1diz.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Inside view of Castillo de Santa Catalina
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Castle_of_Santa_Catalina_(C%C3%A1diz)" title="Castle of Santa Catalina (Cádiz)">
         Castle of Santa Catalina
        </a>
       </i>
       is also a military fortification, and is situated at the end of the Caleta beach. It was built in 1598 following the English sacking of Cádiz two years earlier. Recently renovated, today it is used for exhibitions and concerts.
      </p>

      <p>
       Cádiz has a hot-summer
       <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">
        mediterranean climate
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">
        Köppen
       </a>
       <i>
        Csa
       </i>
       ) with very mild to warm winters and warm to hot summers. The city has significant maritime influences due to its position on a narrow peninsula. Amongst any
       <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">
        European
       </a>
       city, Cádiz has the warmest winters. The annual sunshine hours of Cádiz are above 3000h, being one of the most sunny cities in Europe. Although summer nights are tropical in nature, daytime temperatures are comparatively subdued compared to nearby inland areas such as
       <a href="/wiki/Jerez_de_la_Frontera" title="Jerez de la Frontera">
        Jerez
       </a>
       and the very hot far inland areas in Andalucia. Snowfall is unknown at least since the XIX century, being the least snowy place of Europe.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
