      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Beaches">
        Beaches
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=C%C3%A1diz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Beaches">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Cádiz, situated on a peninsula,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       is home to many beaches.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cadiz_01.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Cadiz_01.jpg/220px-Cadiz_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Cadiz_01.jpg/330px-Cadiz_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Cadiz_01.jpg/440px-Cadiz_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cadiz_01.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         La Caleta Beach
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <i>
        La Playa de
        <a href="/wiki/La_Caleta,_Spain" title="La Caleta, Spain">
         la Caleta
        </a>
       </i>
       is the best-loved beach of Cádiz. It has always been in Carnival songs, due to its unequalled beauty and its proximity to the
       <i>
        Barrio de la Viña
       </i>
       . It is the beach of the Old City, situated between two castles, San Sebastian and Santa Catalina. It is around 400 meters (1,300 ft) long and 30 meters (98 ft) wide at
       <a href="/wiki/Tide" title="Tide">
        low tide
       </a>
       . La Caleta and the boulevard show a lot of resemblance to parts of
       <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">
        Havana
       </a>
       , the capital city of
       <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">
        Cuba
       </a>
       , like the
       <a href="/wiki/Malec%C3%B3n,_Havana" title="Malecón, Havana">
        malecon
       </a>
       . Therefore, it served as the set for several of the Cuban scenes in the beginning of the
       <a href="/wiki/James_Bond" title="James Bond">
        James Bond movie
       </a>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Die_Another_Day" title="Die Another Day">
         Die Another Day
        </a>
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       <i>
        La Playa de la Victoria
       </i>
       , in the newer part of Cádiz, is the beach most visited by tourists and natives of Cádiz. It is about three km long, and it has an average width of 50 meters (160 ft) of sand. The moderate
       <a href="/wiki/Swell_(ocean)" title="Swell (ocean)">
        swell
       </a>
       and the absence of rocks allow family bathing. It is separated from the city by an avenue; on the landward side of the avenue, there are many shops and restaurants.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Catedral_of_Cadiz.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4272" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Catedral_of_Cadiz.jpg/220px-Catedral_of_Cadiz.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Catedral_of_Cadiz.jpg/330px-Catedral_of_Cadiz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Catedral_of_Cadiz.jpg/440px-Catedral_of_Cadiz.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Catedral_of_Cadiz.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         View of the cathedral from Playa de la Santamaría
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <i>
        La Playa de Santa María del Mar
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        Playita de las Mujeres
       </i>
       is a small beach in Cádiz, situated between La Playa de Victoria and La Playa de la Caleta. It features excellent views of the old district of Cádiz.
      </p>
      <p>
       Other beaches are
       <i>
        Torregorda
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Cortadura
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        El Chato
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Carnival">
        Carnival
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=C%C3%A1diz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Carnival">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Carnival_of_C%C3%A1diz" title="Carnival of Cádiz">
        Carnival of Cádiz
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CarnavalCadiz1926.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1338" data-file-width="795" height="370" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/CarnavalCadiz1926.jpg/220px-CarnavalCadiz1926.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/CarnavalCadiz1926.jpg/330px-CarnavalCadiz1926.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/CarnavalCadiz1926.jpg/440px-CarnavalCadiz1926.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CarnavalCadiz1926.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Poster advertising the 1926 Carnival of Cádiz
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Carnival of Cádiz is one of the best known
       <a href="/wiki/Carnival" title="Carnival">
        carnivals
       </a>
       in the world. Throughout the year, carnival-related activities are almost constant in the city; there are always rehearsals, public demonstrations, and
       <a href="/wiki/Competition" title="Competition">
        contests
       </a>
       of various kinds.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Carnival of Cádiz is famous for the satirical groups called
       <i>
        chirigotas
       </i>
       , who perform comical
       <a href="/wiki/Musical_composition" title="Musical composition">
        musical pieces
       </a>
       . Typically, a chirigota is composed of seven to twelve performers who sing, act and improvise accompanied by
       <a href="/wiki/Guitar" title="Guitar">
        guitars
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kazoo" title="Kazoo">
        kazoos
       </a>
       , a
       <a href="/wiki/Bass_drum" title="Bass drum">
        bass drum
       </a>
       , and a variety of noise-makers. Other than the chirigotas, there are many other groups of performers: choruses; ensembles called
       <i>
        comparsas
       </i>
       , who sing in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Close_harmony" title="Close harmony">
        close harmony
       </a>
       much like the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barbershop_quartets" title="Barbershop quartets">
        barbershop quartets
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/African-American_culture" title="African-American culture">
        African-American culture
       </a>
       or the
       <a href="/wiki/Mariachi" title="Mariachi">
        mariachis
       </a>
       of Mexico;
       <i>
        cuartetos
       </i>
       , consisting of four (or sometimes three) performers alternating dramatic parodies and humorous songs; and
       <i>
        romanceros
       </i>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Storytelling" title="Storytelling">
        storytellers
       </a>
       who recite tales in verse. These diverse spectacles turn the city into a colourful and popular open-air theatre for two entire weeks in February.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         Concurso Oficial de Agrupaciones Carnavalescas
        </span>
       </i>
       (the official association of carnival groups) sponsors a contest in the
       <i>
        Gran Teatro Falla
       </i>
       (see above) each year where chirigotas and other performers compete for prizes. This is the climactic event of the Cádiz carnival.
      </p>
      <div style="clear:left;">
      </div>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Gastronomy">
        Gastronomy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=C%C3%A1diz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Gastronomy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tortillita_de_camarones.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Tortillita_de_camarones.jpg/220px-Tortillita_de_camarones.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Tortillita_de_camarones.jpg/330px-Tortillita_de_camarones.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Tortillita_de_camarones.jpg/440px-Tortillita_de_camarones.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tortillita_de_camarones.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <i>
          Tortillita de camarones
         </i>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The gastronomy of Cádiz includes stews and sweets typical of the
       <i>
        comarca
       </i>
       and the city.
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">
        Transportation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=C%C3%A1diz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Transportation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Cádiz is connected to European route
       <a href="/wiki/European_route_E05" title="European route E05">
        E5
       </a>
       which connects it with Sevilla, Cordoba and Madrid to the North and Algeciras to the South East, continuing as
       <a href="/wiki/European_route_E15" title="European route E15">
        E15
       </a>
       northbound along the Spanish mediterranean coast.
      </p>
      <p>
       The city does not have its own airport. The region is served by
       <a href="/wiki/Jerez_Airport" title="Jerez Airport">
        Jerez Airport
       </a>
       , which is approximately 40 km (25 mi) north of the city centre. The airport offers regular domestic flights to Madrid and Barcelona as well as scheduled and seasonal charter flights to the UK, Germany and other European destinations. Local train line C1 connects the airport to Cádiz main train station in 1hr.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The main line train station is located just outside the old town. It offers regional and national services. The connection to the
       <a href="/wiki/Madrid%E2%80%93Seville_high-speed_rail_line" title="Madrid–Seville high-speed rail line">
        Madrid-Seville high-speed rail line
       </a>
       was finished in 2015 after 14 years of construction, which extends the high speed
       <a href="/wiki/Alvia" title="Alvia">
        Alvia
       </a>
       trains to the city. Local services make the outskirts and regional destinations accessible along the line to Jerez and Seville.
      </p>
      <p>
       The port opposite the train station provides weekly ferry services to the
       <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">
        Canary Islands
       </a>
       (2–3 days travel time)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       as well as providing a stop for seasonal cruise ships.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span id="Twin_towns.E2.80.94sister_cities">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns—sister_cities">
        Twin towns—sister cities
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>

         edit

         <li id="cite_note-16">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-16">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           From the
           <i>
            Life of
            <a href="/wiki/Apollonius_of_Tyana" title="Apollonius of Tyana">
             Apollonius of Tyana
            </a>
           </i>
           : " ... the pillars in the temple were made of gold and silver smelted together so as to be of one color, and they were over a cubit high, of square form, resembling anvils; and their capitals were inscribed with letters which were neither Egyptian nor Indian nor of any kind which he could decipher. But Apollonius, since the priests would tell him nothing, remarked: 'Heracles of Egypt does not permit me not to tell all I know. These pillars are ties between earth and ocean, and they were inscribed by Heracles in the house of the Fates, to prevent any discord arising between the elements, and to save their mutual affection for one another from violation.'"
          </span>
